<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="course-objectives">COURSE OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#course-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="broad-objective">BROAD OBJECTIVE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#broad-objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>At the end of the course, the student will be able to acquire knowledge on etiology of various disorders affecting the nervous system, assessment and management of these disorders.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="specific-objectives">SPECIFIC OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>At the end of the course the student will be able to:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Describe management of patient with altered level of consciousness.</li>
<li>Discuss management of patient with increased intracranial pressure.</li>
<li>Utilize Nursing process as a framework in pre and post operative care of patients undergoing intracranial surgery.</li>
<li>Explain management of cerebro vascular disorders in a patient.</li>
</ol>
<p>5.Explain management of patient with infections of the Nervous system.
6. Discuss cranial nerve disorders of the nervous system.
7. Explain the degenerative disorders of the nervous system.
8. Describe management of a patient with trauma to the Nervous system.
9. Discuss the auto immune disorders of the Nervous system.
10. Explain the Oncologic disorders of the nervous system.
11. Describe management of a patient with Epilepsy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="review-of-anatomy-and-physiology-of-ns">REVIEW OF ANATOMY AND PHYSIOLOGY OF NS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#review-of-anatomy-and-physiology-of-ns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The nervous system consists of two divisions: the central nervous system (CNS), including the brain and spinal cord, and the peripheral nervous system, made up of the cranial and spinal nerves.</li>
<li>The peripheral nervous system can be further divided into the</li>
<li>somatic, or voluntary nervous system, and</li>
<li>the autonomic, or involuntary nervous system.</li>
</ul>
<p>The function of the nervous system is to control all motor, sensory, autonomic, cognitive, and behavioral activities</p>
<ul>
<li>The nervous system has approximately 10 million sensory neurons that send information about the internal and external environment to the brain and 500,000 motor neurons that control the muscles and glands.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="neurones">NEURONES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neurones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The basic functional unit of the brain is the neuron.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is composed of a cell body, a dendrite, and an axon.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The <strong>dendrite</strong> is a branch-type structure with synapses for receiving electrochemical messages</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The <strong>axon</strong> is a long projection that carries impulses away from the cell body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nerve cell bodies occurring in clusters are called ganglia or nuclei.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A cluster of cell bodies with the same function is called a center (eg, the respiratory center).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neuroglial cells, another type of nerve cell, support, protect, and nourish neurons.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-124a84e2.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="neurotransmitters">Neurotransmitters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neurotransmitters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Neurotransmitters communicate messages from one neuron to another or from a neuron to a specific target tissue.</li>
<li>Neurotransmitters are manufactured and stored in synaptic vesicles.</li>
<li>They enable conduction of impulses across the synaptic cleft.</li>
</ul>
<p>When released, the neurotransmitter crosses the synaptic cleft and binds to receptors in the postsynaptic cell membrane.</p>
<ul>
<li>The action of a neurotransmitter is to potentiate, terminate, or modulate a specific action and can either excite or inhibit the target cell’s activity</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>Many neurologic disorders are due, at least in part, to an imbalance in neurotransmitters—that is, a lack of gamma aminobutyric acid (GABA) and acetylcholine in Huntington’s disease, low serotonin levels in some forms of epilepsy, and a decrease in dopamine in Parkinson’s disease.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In fact, probably all brain functions are modulated through neurotransmitter receptor site activity, including memory and other cognitive processes.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>They can be excitatory or inhibitory and are rapid-acting (measured in milliseconds).</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Acetylcholine (major transmitter of the parasympathetic nervous system)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Serotonin</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dopamine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Norepinephrine (major transmitter of the sympathetic nervous system)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gamma-aminobutyric acid (GABA)</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anatomy-of-the-brain">ANATOMY OF THE BRAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomy-of-the-brain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The brain is divided into three major areas:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>the cerebrum,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>brain stem, and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>the cerebellum.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The <strong>cerebrum</strong> is composed of two hemispheres, the thalamus, the hypothalamus, and the basal ganglia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cerebrum. The cerebrum consists of two hemispheres that are incompletely separated by the great longitudinal fissure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This sulcus separates the cerebrum into the right and left hemispheres.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The outside surface of the hemispheres has a wrinkled appearance that is the result of many folded layers or convolutions called gyri, which increase the surface area of the brain, accounting for the high level of activity carried out by such a small-appearing organ</p>
<p>The cerebral hemispheres are divided into four parts: frontal, parietal, temporal, and occipital lobes. The four lobes are as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Frontal—the largest lobe. The major functions of this lobe are concentration, abstract thought, information storage or memory, and motor function. It also contains Broca’s area, critical for motor control of speech.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>Parietal—a predominantly sensory lobe. The primary sensory cortex, which analyzes sensory information and relays the interpretation of this information to the thalamus and other cortical areas, is located in the parietal lobe.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Temporal—contains the auditory receptive areas. Contains a vital area called the interpretive area that provides integration of somatization, visual, and auditory areas.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occipital—the posterior lobe of the cerebral hemisphere is responsible for visual interpretation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The corpus callosum is a thick collection of nerve fibers that connects the two hemispheres of the brain and is responsible for the transmission of information from one side of the brain to the other</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The basal ganglia are masses of nuclei located deep in the cerebral hemispheres that are responsible for control of fine motor movements, including those of the hands and lower extremities.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The thalamus lies on either side of the third ventricle and acts primarily as a relay station for all sensation except smell. All memory, sensation, and pain impulses also pass through this section of the brain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The hypothalamus is located anterior and inferior to the thalamus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The hypothalamus lies immediately beneath and lateral to the lower portion of the wall of the third ventricle.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The hypothalamus plays an important role in the endocrine system because it regulates the pituitary secretion of hormones that influence metabolism, reproduction, stress response, and urine production.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It works with the pituitary to maintain fluid balance and maintains temperature regulation by promoting vasoconstriction or vasodilatation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The hypothalamus is the site of the hunger center and is involved in appetite control.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>The pituitary gland is located in the sella turcica at the base of the brain and is connected to the hypothalamus. The pituitary is a common site for brain tumors in adults.</p>
<p>Brain Stem. The brain stem consists of the midbrain, pons, and medulla oblongata.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The midbrain connects the pons and the cerebellum with the cerebral hemispheres; it contains sensory and motor pathways and serves as the center for auditory and visual reflexes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cranial nerves III and IV originate in the midbrain.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>The pons is situated in front of the cerebellum between the midbrain and the medulla and is a bridge between the two halves of the cerebellum, and between the medulla and the cerebrum.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Cranial nerves V through VIII connect to the brain in the pons.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The pons contains motor and sensory pathways. Portions of the pons also control the heart, respiration, and blood pressure.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>The medulla oblongata contains motor fibers from the brain to the spinal cord and sensory fibers from the spinal cord to the brain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cranial nerves IX through XII connect to the brain in the medulla</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Cerebellum. The cerebellum is separated from the cerebral hemispheres by a fold of dura mater, the tentorium cerebelli.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The cerebellum has both excitatory and inhibitory actions and is largely responsible for coordination of movement.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It also controls fine movement, balance, position sense (awareness of where each part of the body is), and integration of sensory input.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="structures-protecting-the-brain">STRUCTURES PROTECTING THE BRAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structures-protecting-the-brain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The brain is contained in the rigid skull, which protects it from injury.</li>
<li>The meninges (fibrous connective tissues that cover the brain and spinal cord) provide protection, support, and nourishment to the brain and spinal cord.</li>
<li>The layers of the meninges are the dura, arachnoid, and pia mater.</li>
</ul>
<p>CEREBROSPINAL FLUID</p>
<ul>
<li>CSF, a clear and colorless fluid with a specific gravity of 1.007, is produced in the ventricles and is circulated around the brain and the spinal cord through the ventricular system.</li>
<li>There are four ventricles: the right and left lateral, and the third and fourth ventricles.</li>
<li>The two lateral ventricles open into the third ventricle at the interventricular foramen or the foramen of Monro.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The third and fourth ventricles connect via the aqueduct of the midbrain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The fourth ventricle supplies CSF to the subarachnoid space and down the spinal cord on the dorsal surface.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>CSF is returned to the brain and is then circulated around the brain, where it is absorbed by the arachnoid villi</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>CSF is produced in the choroid plexus of the lateral, third, and fourth ventricles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The ventricular and subarachnoid system contains approximately 125 to 150 mL of fluid, while 15 to 25 mL of CSF is located in each lateral ventricle.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-b777c448.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cerebral-circulation">CEREBRAL CIRCULATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebral-circulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The cerebral circulation receives approximately 15% of the cardiac output, or 750 mL per minute. The brain does not store nutrients and has a high metabolic demand that requires the high blood flow.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="arteries">Arteries.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arteries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Two internal carotid arteries and two vertebral arteries and their extensive system of branches provide the blood supply to the brain. The internal carotids arise from the bifurcation of the common carotid and supply much of the anterior circulation of the brain.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anatomy-of-the-spinal-cord">ANATOMY OF THE SPINAL CORD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anatomy-of-the-spinal-cord" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The spinal cord and medulla form a continuous structure extending from the cerebral hemispheres and serving as the connection between the brain and the periphery.</li>
<li>Approximately 45 cm (18 in) long and about the thickness of a finger, it extends from the foramen magnum at the base of the skull to the lower border of the first lumbar vertebra, where it tapers to a fibrous band called the conus medullaris.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vertebral-column">VERTEBRAL COLUMN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vertebral-column" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The bones of the vertebral column surround and protect the spinal cord and normally consist of 7 cervical, 12 thoracic, and 5 lumbar vertebrae, as well as the sacrum (a fused mass of five vertebrae), and terminate in the coccyx.</p>
<ul>
<li>Nerve roots exit from the vertebral column through the intervertebral foramina (openings).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-peripheral-nervous-system">The Peripheral Nervous System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-peripheral-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The peripheral nervous system includes the cranial nerves, the spinal nerves, and the autonomic nervous system</li>
<li>There are 12 pairs of cranial nerves that emerge from the lower surface of the brain and pass through the foramina in the skull.</li>
<li>Three are entirely sensory (I, II, VIII), five are motor (III, IV, VI, XI, and XII), and four are mixed (V, VII, IX, and X) as they have both sensory and motor functions</li>
</ul>
<p>The cranial nerves are numbered in the order in which they arise from the brain.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spinal-nerves">SPINAL NERVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-nerves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The spinal cord is composed of 31 pairs of spinal nerves: 8 cervical, 12 thoracic, 5 lumbar, 5 sacral, and 1 coccygeal. Each spinal nerve has a ventral root and a dorsal root</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The dorsal roots are sensory and transmit sensory impulses from specific areas of the body known as dermatomes to the dorsal ganglia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The sensory fiber may be somatic, carrying information about pain, temperature, touch, and position sense (proprioception) from the tendons, joints, and body surfaces; or visceral, carrying information from the internal organs.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The ventral roots are motor and transmit impulses from the spinal cord to the body.</p>
<ul>
<li>These fibers are also either somatic or visceral.</li>
<li>The visceral fibers include autonomic fibers that control the cardiac muscles and glandular secretions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="autonomic-nervous-system">AUTONOMIC NERVOUS SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#autonomic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The autonomic nervous system regulates the activities of internal organs such as the heart, lungs, blood vessels, digestive organs, and glands.</li>
<li>Maintenance and restoration of internal homeostasis is largely the responsibility of the autonomic nervous system.</li>
<li>There are two major divisions: the <strong>sympathetic nervous system</strong>, with predominantly excitatory responses, most notably the “fight or flight” response, and the <strong>parasympathetic nervous system</strong>, which controls mostly visceral functions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lesson-two">LESSON TWO<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lesson-two" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At the end of the lesson, the learner should be able to:</p>
<ol>
<li>explain the components of neurological examination.</li>
<li>Describe diagnostic tests used for assessment of suspected neurologic disorders and the related nursing implications.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-neurologic-examination">The Neurologic Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-neurologic-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-history">HEALTH HISTORY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An important aspect of the neurologic assessment is the history of the present illness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Observing overall appearance, mental status, posture, movement and affect.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Details about the onset, character, severity, location, duration, and frequency of symptoms and signs; associated complaints; precipitating, aggravating, and relieving factors; progression, remission, and exacerbation; and the presence or absence of similar symptoms among family members</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><del>Enquire</del> about any family history of genetic diseases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Included in the health history is a review of the medical history, including a system-by-system evaluation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Enquire about any history of trauma or falls that may have involved the head or spinal cord.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Questions regarding the use of alcohol, medications, and recreational drugs are also asked.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">CLINICAL MANIFESTATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Assess for:</p>
<ul>
<li>Pain</li>
<li>Abnormal Sensation. eg. Numbness, abnormal sensation, or loss of sensation.</li>
<li>Seizures</li>
<li>Seizures are the result of abnormal paroxysmal discharges in the cerebral cortex, which then manifest as an alteration in sensation, behavior, movement, perception, or consciousness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dizziness">Dizziness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dizziness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Dizziness is an abnormal sensation of imbalance or movement.</li>
<li>It is fairly common in the elderly and one of the most common complaints encountered by health professionals.</li>
<li>Vertigo, a specific form of dizziness, is defined as a sensation that is usually a manifestation of vestibular dysfunction.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="visual-disturbances">Visual Disturbances<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#visual-disturbances" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Lesions of the eye itself (eg, cataract), lesions along the pathway (eg, tumor), or lesions in the visual cortex (from stroke) interfere with normal visual acuity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Abnormalities of eye movement (as in the nystagmus associated with multiple sclerosis) can also compromise vision by causing diplopia or double vision.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weakness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weakness, specifically muscle weakness, is a common manifestation of neurologic disease</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="physical-examination">PHYSICAL EXAMINATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A neurologic assessment is divided into five components:</li>
<li>Cerebral function,</li>
<li>Cranial nerves,</li>
<li>Motor system,</li>
<li>Sensory system, and</li>
<li>Reflexes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessing-cerebral-function">Assessing Cerebral Function<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessing-cerebral-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cerebral abnormalities may cause disturbances in mental status, intellectual functioning, and thought content and in patterns of emotional behavior.</li>
<li>There may also be alterations in perception, motor and language abilities, as well as lifestyle.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-mental-status">1. MENTAL STATUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-mental-status" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>An assessment of mental status begins by observing the patient's appearance and behavior, noting dress, grooming, and personal hygiene.</li>
<li>Posture, gestures, movements, facial expressions, and motor activity often provide important information about the patient.</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient's manner of speech and level of consciousness are also assessed. Is the patient's speech clear and coherent?</p>
<ul>
<li>Is the patient alert and responsive, or drowsy and stuporous?</li>
<li>Assessing orientation to time, place, and person assists in evaluating mental status.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="intellectual-function">INTELLECTUAL FUNCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intellectual-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A person with an average IQ can subtract seven digits without faltering from 100 and can recite five digits backward from 100.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="thought-content">THOUGHT CONTENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thought-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>During the interview, it is important to assess the patient's thought content. Are the patient's thoughts spontaneous, natural, clear, relevant, and coherent?</li>
<li>Does the patient have any fixed ideas or illusions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="emotional-status">EMOTIONAL STATUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emotional-status" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is the patient’s affect (external manifestation of mood) natural and even, or irritable and angry, anxious, apathetic or flat, or euphoric.</li>
<li>Does his or her mood fluctuate normally, or does the patient unpredictably swing from joy to sadness</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="perception">PERCEPTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#perception" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The examiner may now consider more specific areas of higher cortical function. Agnosia is the inability to interpret or recognize objects seen through the special senses.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient may see a pencil but not know what it is called or what to do with it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient may even be able to describe it but not to interpret its function</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Type of Agnosia Area</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Visual</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Auditory</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tactile</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Body parts and relationships</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="affected-cerebral">Affected Cerebral<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#affected-cerebral" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Occipital lobe</li>
<li>Temporal lobe</li>
<li>Parietal lobe</li>
<li>Parietal lobe</li>
</ul>
<p>LANGUAGE ABILITY</p>
<ul>
<li>The person with normal neurologic function can understand and communicate in spoken and written language.</li>
<li>Does the patient answer questions appropriately?</li>
<li>Can he or she read a sentence from a newspaper and explain its meaning? Can the patient write his or her name or copy a simple figure that the examiner has drawn?</li>
<li>A deficiency in language function is called aphasia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Type of Aphasia</li>
<li>Auditory-receptive</li>
<li>Visual-receptive</li>
<li>Expressive speaking</li>
<li>Expressive writing</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="brain-area-involved">Brain Area Involved<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#brain-area-involved" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Temporal lobe</p>
<p>Parietal-occipital area</p>
<p>frontal areas</p>
<p>Posterior frontal area</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="impact-on-lifestyle">IMPACT ON LIFESTYLE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#impact-on-lifestyle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The nurse assesses the impact the neurologic impairment has on the patient's lifestyle.</li>
<li>Issues to consider include the limitations imposed on the patient by any deficit and the patient's role in society, including family and community roles.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="examining-the-cranial-nerves">Examining the Cranial Nerves<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examining-the-cranial-nerves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>I (olfactory):</p>
<ul>
<li>With eyes closed, the patient identifies familiar odors (coffee, tobacco). Each nostril is tested separately</li>
</ul>
<p>II (optic)</p>
<ul>
<li>Snellen eye chart; visual fields; ophthalmoscopic examination</li>
</ul>
<p>For cranial nerves III, IV, and VI: test for ocular rotations, conjugate movements, nystagmus. Test for pupillary reflexes, and inspect eyelids for ptosis.</p>
<p>V (trigeminal)</p>
<ul>
<li>Have patient close the eyes. Touch cotton to forehead, cheeks, and jaw.</li>
<li>Sensitivity to superficial pain is tested by using the sharp and dull ends of a broken tongue blade. Alternate between the sharp point and the dull end. Patient reports "sharp" or "dull" with each movement.</li>
</ul>
<p>While the patient looks up, lightly touch a wisp of cotton against the temporal surface of each cornea. A blink and tearing are normal responses.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Have the patient clench and move the jaw from side to side.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Facial: Observe for symmetry while the patient performs facial movements: smiles, whistles, elevates eyebrows, frowns, tightly closes eyelids against resistance (examiner attempts to open them).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Observe face for flaccid paralysis (shallow naso labial folds).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Patient extends tongue. Ability to discriminate between sugar and salt is tested.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acoustic">ACOUSTIC:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acoustic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Whisper test</li>
<li>Test for lateralization (Weber)</li>
<li>Test for air and bone conduction (Rinne)</li>
</ul>
<p>Glosso pharngeal:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Assess patient’s ability to discriminate between sugar and salt on posterior third of the tongue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assess for swallowing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vagus: Depress a tongue blade on posterior tongue, or stimulate posterior pharynx to elicit gag reflex.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Note any hoarseness in voice.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Have patient say “ah.” Observe for symmetric rise of uvula and soft palate.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="spinal-accessory">SPINAL ACCESSORY:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-accessory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Palpate and note strength of trapezius muscles while patient shrugs shoulders against resistance.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Palpate and note strength of each sternocleidomastoid muscle as patient turns head against opposing pressure of the examiner’s hand.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypoglossal: While the patient protrudes the tongue, any deviation or tremors are noted.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The strength of the tongue is tested by having the patient move the protruded tongue from side to side against a tongue depressor.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="examining-the-motor-system">Examining the Motor System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examining-the-motor-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A thorough examination of the motor system includes an assessment of muscle size, tone, and strength, coordination, and balance.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient is instructed to walk across the room while the examiner observes posture and gait.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The muscles are inspected, and palpated if necessary, for their size and symmetry.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Any evidence of atrophy or involuntary movements (tremors, tics) is noted.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Abnormalities in tone include spasticity (increased muscle tone),</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>rigidity (resistance to passive stretch), and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>flaccidity</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="muscle-strength">MUSCLE STRENGTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#muscle-strength" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Assessing the patient's ability to flex or extend the extremities against resistance tests muscle strength.</li>
<li>Clinicians use a five-point scale to rate muscle strength.</li>
<li>A 5 indicates full power of contraction against gravity and resistance or normal muscle strength;</li>
<li>4 indicates fair but not full strength against gravity and a moderate amount of resistance or slight weakness;</li>
</ul>
<p>3 indicates just sufficient strength to overcome the force of gravity or moderate weakness;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>2 indicates the ability to move but not to overcome the force of gravity or severe weakness;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1 indicates minimal contractile power—weak muscle contraction noted—or very severe weakness; and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>0 indicates complete paralysis.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="balance-and-coordination">BALANCE AND COORDINATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#balance-and-coordination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Cerebellar influence on the motor system is reflected in balance control and coordination.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Coordination in the hands and upper extremities is tested by having the patient perform rapid, alternating movements and point-to-point testing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ataxia is defined as in coordination of voluntary muscle action, particularly of the muscle groups used in activities such as walking or reaching for objects</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The presence of ataxia or tremors (rhythmic, involuntary movements) during these movements suggests cerebellar disease.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The Romberg test is a screening test for balance.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The patient stands with feet together and arms at the side, first with eyes open and then with both eyes closed for 20 to 30 seconds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The examiner stands close to reassure the patient of support if he or she begins to fall.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Slight swaying is normal, but a loss of balance is abnormal and is considered a positive Romberg test.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="examining-the-reflexes">Examining the Reflexes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examining-the-reflexes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The motor reflexes are involuntary contractions of muscles or muscle groups in response to abrupt stretching near the site of the muscle’s insertion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The tendon is struck directly with a reflex hammer or indirectly by striking the examiner’s thumb, which is placed firmly against the tendon.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Testing these reflexes enables the examiner to assess involuntary reflex arcs that depend on the presence of afferent stretch receptors, spinal synapses, efferent motor fibers, and a variety of modifying influences from higher levels.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Common reflexes that may be tested include the deep tendon reflexes (biceps, brachio radialis, triceps, patellar, and ankle reflexes) and Superficial reflexes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Deep tendon reflexes are graded on a scale of 0 to 4:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>0 No response</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>1+ Diminished (hypoactive)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>2+ Normal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>3+ Increased (may be interpreted as normal)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>4+ Hyperactive (hyperreflexia)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The major superficial reflexes include corneal, gag or swallowing, upper/lower abdominal, cremasteric (men only), plantar, and perianal.</p>
<p>These reflexes are graded differently than the motor reflexes and are noted to be present (+) or absent (-).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sensory-examination">Sensory Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sensory-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The sensory examination is largely subjective and requires the cooperation of the patient.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assessment of the sensory system involves tests for tactile sensation, superficial pain, vibration, and position sense (proprioception).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>During the sensory assessment, the patient's eyes are closed..</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tactile sensation is assessed by lightly touching a cotton wisp to corresponding areas on each side of the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Determining the patient’s sensitivity to a sharp object can assess superficial pain perception.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient is asked to differentiate between the sharp and dull ends of a broken wooden tongue blade; using a safety pin is inadvisable because it breaks the skin.</p>
<ul>
<li>Vibration may be evaluated through the use of a low-frequency tuning fork.</li>
<li>The handle of the vibrating fork is placed against a bony prominence, and the patient is asked whether he or she feels a sensation and is instructed to signal the examiner when the sensation ceases.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="position-sense-or-proprioception-may-be-determined-by-asking-the-patient-to-close-both-eyes-and-indicate-as-the-great-toe-is-alternately-moved-up-and-down-in-which-direction-movement-has-taken-place">Position sense or proprioception may be determined by asking the patient to close both eyes and indicate, as the great toe is alternately moved up and down, in which direction movement has taken place.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#position-sense-or-proprioception-may-be-determined-by-asking-the-patient-to-close-both-eyes-and-indicate-as-the-great-toe-is-alternately-moved-up-and-down-in-which-direction-movement-has-taken-place" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-tests">DIAGNOSTIC TESTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>COMPUTED TOMOGRAPHY SCANNING</strong></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Computed tomography (CT) makes use of a narrow x-ray beam to scan the head in successive layers.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The images provide cross sectional views of the brain, with distinguishing differences in tissue densities of the skull, cortex, sub cortical structures, and ventricles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lesions in the brain are seen as variations in tissue density differing from the surrounding normal brain tissue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Abnormalities of tissue indicate possible tumor masses, brain infarction, displacement of the ventricles, and cortical atrophy.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="positron-emission-tomography">POSITRON EMISSION TOMOGRAPHY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#positron-emission-tomography" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It is a computer-based nuclear imaging technique that produces images of actual organ functioning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient either inhales a radioactive gas or is injected with a radioactive substance that emits positively charged particles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When these positrons combine with negatively charged electrons (normally found in the body’s cells), the resultant gamma rays can be detected by a scanning device that produces a series of two-dimensional views at various levels of the brain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This information is integrated by a computer and gives a composite picture of the brain at work.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>PET permits the measurement of blood flow, tissue composition, and brain metabolism and thus indirectly evaluates brain function.</p>
<p>This test is useful in showing metabolic changes in the brain (Alzheimer’s disease), locating lesions (brain tumor, epileptogenic lesions), identifying blood flow and oxygen metabolism in patients with strokes,</p>
<p>evaluating new therapies for brain tumors, and revealing biochemical abnormalities associated with mental illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="magnetic-resonance-imaging">MAGNETIC RESONANCE IMAGING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#magnetic-resonance-imaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) uses a powerful magnetic field to obtain images of different areas of the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This diagnostic test involves altering hydrogen ions in the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Placing the patient into a powerful magnetic field causes the hydrogen nuclei (protons) within the body to align like small magnets in a magnetic field.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>MRI has the potential for identifying a cerebral abnormality earlier and more clearly than other diagnostic tests.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It can provide information about the chemical changes within cells, allowing the clinician to monitor a tumor’s response to treatment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is particularly useful in the diagnosis of multiple sclerosis and can describe the activity and extent of disease in the brain and spinal cord.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>MRI does not involve ionizing radiation</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cerebral-angiography">CEREBRAL ANGIOGRAPHY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebral-angiography" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Cerebral angiography is an x-ray study of the cerebral circulation with a contrast agent injected into a selected artery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cerebral angiography is a valuable tool to investigate vascular disease, aneurysms, and arteriovenous malformations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is frequently performed before craniotomy to assess the patency and adequacy of the cerebral circulation and to determine the site, size, and nature of the pathologic processes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Most cerebral angiograms are performed by threading a catheter through the femoral artery in the groin and up to the desired vessel.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Alternatively, direct puncture of the carotid or vertebral artery or retrograde injection of a contrast agent into the brachial artery may be performed.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="myelography">MYELOGRAPHY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#myelography" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A myelogram is an x-ray of the spinal subarachnoid space taken after the injection of a contrast agent into the spinal subarachnoid space through a lumbar puncture.</li>
<li>It outlines the spinal subarachnoid space and shows any distortion of the spinal cord or spinal dural sac caused by tumors, cysts, herniated vertebral disk.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="electroencephalography">ELECTROENCEPHALOGRAPHY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electroencephalography" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It is a non invasive procedure that provides a physiologic assessment of cerebral activity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An electroencephalogram (EEG) represents a record of the electrical activity generated in the brain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is obtained through electrodes applied on the scalp or through microelectrodes placed within the brain tissue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Electrodes are applied to the scalp to record the electrical activity in various regions of the brain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The amplified activity of the neurons between any two of these electrodes is recorded on continuously moving paper; this record is called the encephalogram</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lumbar-puncture-and-examination-of-cerebrospinal-fluid">LUMBAR PUNCTURE AND EXAMINATION OF CEREBROSPINAL FLUID<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lumbar-puncture-and-examination-of-cerebrospinal-fluid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A lumbar puncture (spinal tap) is carried out by inserting a needle into the lumbar subarachnoid space to withdraw CSF.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The needle is usually inserted into the subarachnoid space between the third and fourth or fourth and fifth lumbar vertebrae.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Because the spinal cord divides into a sheaf of nerves at the first lumbar vertebra, insertion of the needle below the level of the third lumbar vertebra prevents puncture of the spinal cord</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indications-of-lp">INDICATIONS OF LP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications-of-lp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>To obtain CSF for examination</li>
<li>To measure and reduce CSF pressure,</li>
<li>To determine the presence or absence of blood in the CSF,</li>
<li>To detect spinal subarachnoid block, and</li>
<li>To administer antibiotics intrathecally (into the spinal canal) in certain cases of infection</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: A lumbar puncture may be risky in the presence of an intracranial mass lesion because intracranial pressure is decreased by the removal of CSF, and the brain may herniate downward through the tentorium and the foramen magnum.</p>
<p>LP is also CONTRA INDICATED in patients with increased intracranial pressure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cerebrospinal-fluid-analysis">Cerebrospinal Fluid Analysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebrospinal-fluid-analysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The CSF should be clear and colorless.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pink, blood-tinged, or grossly bloody CSF may indicate a cerebral contusion, laceration, or subarachnoid hemorrhage.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sometimes with a difficult lumbar puncture, the CSF initially is bloody because of local trauma but then becomes clearer</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The specimens are obtained for cell count, culture, and glucose and protein testing</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications-of-lp">COMPLICATIONS OF LP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-lp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A post-lumbar puncture headache, ranging from mild to severe, may appear a few hours to several days after the procedure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This is the most common complication, occurring in 15% to 30% of patients.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is a throbbing bi frontal or occipital headache, dull and deep in character.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is particularly severe on sitting or standing but lessens or disappears when the patient lies down.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The headache is caused by CSF leakage at the puncture site.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The post puncture headache is usually managed by bed rest, analgesic agents, and hydration.</p>
<ul>
<li>Occasionally, if the headache persists, the epidural blood patch technique may be used.</li>
<li>Blood is withdrawn from the antecubital vein and injected into the epidural space, usually at the site of the previous spinal puncture.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-complications">Other complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Herniation of the intracranial contents</li>
<li>spinal epidural abscess,</li>
<li>spinal epidural hematoma, and</li>
<li>meningitis; a rare but serious complications of lumbar puncture.</li>
<li>temporary voiding problems,</li>
<li>slight elevation of temperature,</li>
<li>backache or spasms, and stiffness of the neck.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="guidelines-for-assisting-with-a-lumbar-puncture">Guidelines for Assisting with a Lumbar Puncture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#guidelines-for-assisting-with-a-lumbar-puncture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pre-procedure">Pre procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Determine whether written consent for the procedure has been obtained.</li>
<li>Explain the procedure to the patient and describe sensations that are likely during the procedure (ie, a sensation of cold as the site is cleansed with solution, a needle prick when local anesthetic is injected).</li>
</ol>
<p>Determine whether the patient has any questions or misconceptions about the procedure; reassure the patient that the needle will not enter the spinal cord or cause paralysis.
4. Instruct the patient to void before the procedure</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure-performed-by-the-physician">Procedure (performed by the physician)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure-performed-by-the-physician" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>The patient is positioned on one side at the edge of the bed or examining table with back toward the physician; the thighs and legs are flexed as much as possible to increase the space between the spinous processes of the vertebrae, for easier entry into the subarachnoid space</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A small pillow may be placed under the patient's head to maintain the spine in a horizontal position; a pillow may be placed between the legs to prevent the upper leg from rolling forward</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nurse assists the patient to maintain the position to avoid sudden movement, which can produce a traumatic (bloody) tap.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient is encouraged to relax and is instructed to breathe normally, because hyperventilation may lower an elevated pressure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nurse describes the procedure step by step to the patient as it proceeds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The physician cleanses the puncture site with an antiseptic solution and drapes the site.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Local anesthetic is injected to numb the puncture site, and then a spinal needle is inserted into the subarachnoid space through the third and fourth or fourth and fifth lumbar interspace.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A specimen of CSF is removed and usually collected in three test tubes, labeled in order of collection. A pressure reading may be obtained. The needle is withdrawn.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A small dressing is applied to the puncture site.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The tubes of CSF are sent to the laboratory immediately</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="post-lumbar-puncture">POST LUMBAR PUNCTURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-lumbar-puncture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Instruct the patient to lie prone for 2 to 3 hours to separate the alignment of the dural and arachnoid needle punctures in the meninges, to reduce leakage of CSF.</li>
<li>Monitor the patient for complications of lumbar puncture; notify physician if complications occur.</li>
<li>Encourage increased fluid intake to reduce the risk of post procedure headache</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-patients-with-neurologic-disorders">MANAGEMENT OF PATIENTS WITH NEUROLOGIC DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-patients-with-neurologic-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="altered-level-of-consciousness">ALTERED LEVEL OF CONSCIOUSNESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#altered-level-of-consciousness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>At the end of the lesson the learner should be able to:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Define altered level of consciousness</li>
<li>Describe the multiple needs of the patient with altered level of consciousness.</li>
<li>Use the nursing process as a framework for care of the patient with altered level of consciousness.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">INTRODUCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>An altered level of consciousness (LOC) refers to a state in which the patient is not oriented, does not follow commands, or needs persistent stimuli to achieve a state of alertness.</li>
<li>LOC is gauged on a continuum with a normal state of alertness and full cognition (consciousness) on one end and coma on the other end.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="terminologies">TERMINOLOGIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terminologies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Coma: It is a clinical state of unconsciousness in which the patient is unaware of self or the environment for prolonged periods (days to months or even years).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Akinetic mutism: A state of unresponsiveness to the environment in which the patient makes no movement or sound but sometimes opens the eyes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Persistent vegetative state: It is a condition in which the patient is described as wakeful but devoid of conscious content, without cognitive or affective mental function.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Altered LOC is not a disorder itself; rather, it is a function and symptom of multiple pathophysiologic phenomena. The cause may be:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Neurologic (head injury, stroke)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Toxicologic (drug overdose, alcohol intoxication),</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Metabolic (hepatic or renal failure, diabetic ketoacidosis).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intact anatomic structures of the brain are needed for proper function.</p>
</li>
<li>
