<p>The two hemispheres of the cerebrum must communicate, via an intact corpus callosum, and the lobes of the brain (frontal, parietal, temporal, and occipital) must communicate and coordinate their specific functions</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The brain stem contains areas that control the heart, respiration, and blood pressure.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Disruptions in the anatomic structures are caused by trauma, edema, pressure from tumors as well as other mechanisms such as an increase or decrease in blood or cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) circulation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All these causes leads to altered level of consciousness.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This causes of neurologic disruption in the cells of the nervous system, neurotransmitters, or brain anatomy.</li>
<li>A disruption in the basic functional units (neurons) or neurotransmitters results in faulty impulse transmission, impeding communication within the brain or from the brain to other parts of the body</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>As the patient’s state of alertness and consciousness decreases, there will be changes in the pupillary response, eye opening response, verbal response, and motor response.
(Components of glass gow coma scale).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Initial changes may be reflected by subtle behavioral changes such as restlessness or increased anxiety.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The pupils become sluggish (response to light is slower); as the patient becomes comatose, the pupils become fixed (no response to light).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient in a coma does not open the eyes, respond verbally, or move the extremities in response to a request to do so.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A complete assessment is performed, with particular attention to the neurologic system.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The neurologic examination should be as complete as the LOC allows.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It includes an evaluation of mental status, cranial nerve function, cerebellar function (balance and coordination), reflexes, and motor and sensory function.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>LOC, a sensitive indicator of neurologic function, is assessed based on the criteria in the Glasgow Coma Scale: eye opening, verbal response, and motor response.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient’s responses are rated on a scale from 3 to 15.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A score of 15 indicates that the patient is fully responsive</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A score of 3 indicates severe impairment of neurologic function</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="glasgow-coma-scale">Glasgow Coma Scale<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glasgow-coma-scale" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Eye opening response</p>
<ul>
<li>Spontaneous 4</li>
<li>To voice 3</li>
<li>To pain 2</li>
<li>None 1</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="verbal-response">Verbal response<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#verbal-response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Oriented 5</li>
<li>Confused 4</li>
<li>Inappropriate words 3</li>
<li>Incomprehensible sounds 2</li>
<li>None 1</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="best-motor-response">Best motor response<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#best-motor-response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Obeys command 6</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Localizes pain 5</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Withdraws 4</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Flexion 3</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Extension 2</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>No response 1</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the patient is comatose, with localized signs such as abnormal pupillary and motor responses, it is assumed that neurologic disease is present until proven otherwise.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the patient is comatose and pupillary light reflexes are preserved, a toxic or metabolic disorder is suspected.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-tests">Diagnostic tests<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Procedures used to identify the cause of unconsciousness include:</p>
<ul>
<li>computed tomography,</li>
<li>magnetic resonance imaging,</li>
<li>positron emission tomography,</li>
<li>and electroencephalography</li>
</ul>
<p>Laboratory tests incude:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>analysis of blood glucose,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>electrolytes,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>serum ammonia, and blood urea nitrogen levels,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>calcium level,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Partial thromboplastin and prothrombin times.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Other studies may be used to evaluate serum ketones and alcohol, drug levels, and arterial blood gas levels.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The first priority of treatment for the patient with altered LOC is to obtain and maintain a patent airway.</li>
<li>The patient may be orally or nasally intubated, or a tracheostomy may be performed until the patient’s ability to breathe on his or her own is determined,</li>
<li><del>A mechanical ventilator is used to maintain adequate oxygenation.</del></li>
</ul>
<p>The circulatory status (blood pressure, heart rate) is monitored to ensure adequate perfusion to the body and brain.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An intravenous catheter is inserted to provide access for fluids and intravenous medications.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neurologic care focuses on the specific neurologic pathology, if any.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutritional support, using either a feeding tube or a gastrostomy tube, is initiated as soon as possible.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In addition to measures to determine and treat the underlying causes of altered LOC.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>other medical interventions are aimed at pharmacologic management of complications and strategies to prevent complications.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Potential complications include:</li>
<li>Respiratory failure,</li>
<li>Pneumonia,</li>
<li>Pressure ulcers, and</li>
<li>Aspiration.</li>
<li>venous stasis,</li>
<li>musculoskeletal deterioration,</li>
<li>disturbed gastrointestinal functioning.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-process">NURSING PROCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Assessment:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assessing the verbal response. Determining the patient’s orientation to time, person, and place.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient is asked to identify the day, date, or season of the year and to identify where he or she is or to identify the clinicians, family members, or visitors present. (Not done when a patient is intubated or has tracheostomy.)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Alertness is measured by the patient’s ability to open the eyes spontaneously or to a stimulus. Patients with severe neurologic dysfunction cannot do this.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nurse should assess for periorbital edema or trauma, which may prevent the patient from opening the eyes, and document.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Motor response includes spontaneous, purposeful movement (eg, the awake patient can move all four extremities with equal strength),</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Movement only in response to noxious stimuli (eg, pressure/pain), or abnormal posturing is noted.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>If the patient is not responding to commands, the motor response is tested by applying a painful stimulus (firm but gentle pressure) to the nail bed or by squeezing a muscle.
In addition to LOC, the nurse monitors parameters such as respiratory status, eye signs, and reflexes on an ongoing basis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Ineffective airway clearance related to altered level of consciousness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Risk of injury related to decreased level of consciousness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Deficient fluid volume related to inability to take in fluids by mouth.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Risk for impaired skin integrity related to immobility.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Impaired tissue integrity of cornea related to diminished or absent corneal reflex</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ineffective thermoregulation related to damage to hypothalamic center</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Impaired urinary elimination (incontinence or retention) related to impairment in neurologic sensing and control.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Impaired oral mucous membranes related to mouth breathing, absence of pharyngeal reflex, and altered fluid intake.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="plans-goals">PLANS/GOALS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#plans-goals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The goals of care for the patient with altered LOC include</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maintenance of a clear airway,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>protection from injury,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>attainment of fluid volume balance,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>achievement of intact oral mucous membranes,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>maintenance of normal skin integrity,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>absence of corneal irritation,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>attainment of effective thermoregulation,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>effective urinary elimination</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-interventions">Nursing Interventions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>MAINTAINING THE AIRWAY</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Elevating the head of the bed to 30 degrees helps prevent aspiration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Positioning the patient in a lateral or semiprone position will also help as it permits the jaw and tongue to fall forward, thus promoting drainage of secretions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Positioning alone is not always adequate,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient may require suctioning and oral hygiene.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Suctioning is performed to remove secretions from the posterior pharynx and upper trachea</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>chest physiotherapy and postural drainage may be initiated to promote pulmonary hygiene, unless contraindicated by the patient’s underlying condition.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Also, the chest should be auscultated at least every 8 hours to detect adventitious breath sounds or absence of breath sounds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Patient with altered LOC also requires intubation and mechanical ventilation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nursing actions for the mechanically ventilated patient include maintaining the patency of the endotracheal tube or tracheostomy, providing frequent oral care, monitoring arterial blood gas measurements, and maintaining ventilator settings</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="protecting-the-patient">PROTECTING THE PATIENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protecting-the-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>For the protection of the patient, padded siderails are provided and raised at all times.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Care should be taken to prevent injury from invasive lines and equipment, and other potential sources of injury should be identified</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Protection also encompasses the concept of protecting the patient's dignity during altered LOC.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Simple measures such as providing privacy and speaking to the patient during nursing care activities preserve the patient's humanity</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maintaining-fluid-balance-and-managing-nutritional-needs">MAINTAINING FLUID BALANCE AND MANAGING NUTRITIONAL NEEDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintaining-fluid-balance-and-managing-nutritional-needs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Hydration status is assessed by examining tissue turgor and mucous membranes, assessing intake and output trends, and analyzing laboratory data.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><del>Fluid</del> needs are met initially by giving the required fluids intravenously.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>However, intravenous solutions (and blood transfusions) for patients with intracranial conditions must be administered slowly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If given too rapidly, they may increase ICP.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The quantity of fluids administered may be restricted to minimize the possibility of producing cerebral edema.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="providing-mouth-care">PROVIDING MOUTH CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#providing-mouth-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The mouth is inspected for dryness, inflammation, and crusting.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The mouth is cleansed and rinsed carefully to remove secretions and crusts and to keep the mucous membranes moist.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A thin coating of petrolatum on the lips prevents drying, cracking, and encrustations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the patient has an endo tracheal tube, the tube should be moved to the opposite side of the mouth daily to prevent ulceration of the mouth and lips</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maintaining-skin-and-joint-integrity">MAINTAINING SKIN AND JOINT INTEGRITY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maintaining-skin-and-joint-integrity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There should be regular schedule of turning to avoid pressure, which can cause breakdown and necrosis of the skin.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preserving-corneal-integrity">PRESERVING CORNEAL INTEGRITY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preserving-corneal-integrity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Some unconscious patients have their eyes open and have inadequate or absent corneal reflexes.</li>
<li>The cornea is likely to become irritated or scratched, leading to keratitis and corneal ulcers.</li>
</ul>
<p>The eyes may be cleansed with cotton balls moistened with sterile normal saline to remove debris and discharge.</p>
<ul>
<li>If artificial tears are prescribed, they may be instilled every 2 hours.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="achieving-thermoregulation">ACHIEVING THERMOREGULATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#achieving-thermoregulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>High fever in the unconscious patient may be caused by infection of the respiratory or urinary tract, drug reactions, or damage to the hypothalamic temperature-regulating center.</li>
<li>Persistent hyperthermia with no identified clinical source of infection indicates brain stem damage and a poor prognosis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3322db0f">Strategies för reducera fevärd<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3322db0f" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Removing all bedding över the patient (with the possible exception of a light sheet or small drape)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administering repeated doses of acetaminophen as prescribed</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Giving a cool sponge bath and allowing an electric fan to blow over the patient to increase surface cooling</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Using a hypothermia blanket</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Frequent temperature monitoring is indicated to assess the response to the therapy and to prevent an excessive decrease in temperature and shivering</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preventing-urinary-retention">PREVENTING URINARY RETENTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preventing-urinary-retention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The patient with an altered LOC is often incontinent or has urinary retention.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The bladder is palpated or scanned at intervals to determine whether urinary retention is present, because a full bladder may be an overlooked cause of overflow incontinence</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Initially an indwelling urinary catheter attached to a closed drainage system is inserted.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A catheter may be inserted during the acute phase of illness to monitor urinary output.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="promoting-bowel-function">PROMOTING BOWEL FUNCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#promoting-bowel-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Immobility and lack of dietary fiber may cause constipation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nurse monitors the number and consistency of bowel movements and performs a rectal examination for signs of fecal impaction.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stool softeners may be prescribed and can be administered with tube feedings</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To facilitate bowel emptying, a glycerine suppository may be indicated.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient may require an enema every other day to empty the lower colon.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="monitoring-and-managing-potential-complications">MONITORING AND MANAGING POTENTIAL COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monitoring-and-managing-potential-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Pneumonia, aspiration, and respiratory failure are potential complications in any patient who has a depressed LOC and who cannot protect the airway or turn, cough, and take deep breaths.</p>
<p>The longer the period of unconsciousness, the greater the risk for pulmonary complications.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Vital signs and respiratory function are monitored closely to detect any signs of respiratory failure or distress</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chest physiotherapy and suctioning are initiated to prevent respiratory complications such as pneumonia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If pneumonia develops, cultures are obtained to identify the organism so that appropriate antibiotics can be administered.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient should also be monitored for signs and symptoms of deep vein thrombosis.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Patients who develop deep vein thrombosis are at risk for pulmonary embolism.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prophylaxis such as subcutaneous heparin or low-molecular-weight heparin is administered.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="evaluation">Evaluation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#evaluation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Maintains clear airway and demonstrates appropriate breath sounds</li>
<li>Experiences no injuries</li>
<li>Attains/maintains adequate fluid status</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>a. Has no clinical signs or symptoms of dehydration</li>
<li>b. Demonstrates normal range of serum electrolytes</li>
<li>c. Has no clinical signs or symptoms of overhydration</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>
<p>Attains/maintains healthy oral mucous membranes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maintains normal skin integrity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has no corneal irritation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Attains or maintains thermoregulation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has no urinary retention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has no diarrhea or fecal impaction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is free of complications</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>a. Has arterial blood gas values within normal range
b. Displays no signs or symptoms of pneumonia
c. Exhibits intact skin over pressure areas
d. Does not develop deep vein thrombosis</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="increased-intracranial-pressure">Increased Intracranial Pressure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#increased-intracranial-pressure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>At the end of the lesson, the student should be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the patho physiology of increased Intracranial pressure.</li>
<li>Identify the early and late clinical manifestations of increased intracranial pressure.</li>
<li>Explain management of a patient with increased ICP.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">INTRODUCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The rigid cranial vault contains brain tissue (1,400 g), blood (75 mL), and CSF (75 mL).</li>
<li>The volume and pressure of these three components are usually in a state of equilibrium and produce the ICP.</li>
<li>ICP is usually measured in the lateral ventricles; normal ICP is 10 to 20 mm Hg</li>
</ul>
<p>The Monro-Kellie hypothesis states that because of the limited space for expansion within the skull, an increase in any one of the components causes a change in the volume of the others.</p>
<p>Because brain tissue has limited space to change, compensation typically is accomplished by:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>displacing or shifting CSF,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>increasing the absorption of CSF, or</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>decreasing cerebral blood volume</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Increased ICP is a syndrome that affects many patients with acute neurologic conditions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Increased ICP affects patient with acute neural conditions and is normally caused by:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>head injury and also it may be seen as a secondary effect in other conditions, such as</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>brain tumors,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>subarachnoid hemorrhage, and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>toxic and viral encephalopathies</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Increased ICP from any cause decreases cerebral perfusion, stimulates further swelling (edema), and shifts brain tissue through openings in the rigid dura, resulting in herniation, a dire, frequently fatal event.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="decreased-cerebral-blood-flow">DECREASED CEREBRAL BLOOD FLOW<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#decreased-cerebral-blood-flow" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Increased ICP may significantly reduce cerebral blood flow, resulting in ischemia and cell death.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the early stages of cerebral ischemia, the vasomotor centers are stimulated and the systemic pressure rises to maintain cerebral blood flow.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Usually a slow bounding pulse and respiratory irregularities accompany this.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These changes in blood pressure, pulse, and respiration are important clinically because they suggest increased ICP.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cerebral-edema">CEREBRAL EDEMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebral-edema" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cerebral edema or swelling is defined as an abnormal accumulation of water or fluid in the intracellular space, extracellular space, or both, associated with an increase in brain tissue volume.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">CLINICAL MANIFESTATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="early-clinical-manifestations">Early clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any sudden change in patient’s behavior to include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Disorientation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Restlessness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>confusion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Increasing drowsiness,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Increased Respiratory effort</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pupillary changes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Headache that is constant, increasing in intensity and aggravated by movement or straining.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weakness in one extremity or one side of the body.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="later-signs-of-increasing-icp">Later signs of increasing ICP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#later-signs-of-increasing-icp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Decreasing level of consciousness until the patient is comatose</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pulse rate and respiratory rate decreases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Blood pressure increases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Temperature increases</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><del>Altered respiratory patterns including Cheyne-Stokes breathing</del></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Projectile vomiting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Loss of brain stem reflexes eg. pupillary, gag, swallowing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hemiplegic.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The patient may undergo:</p>
<ul>
<li>cerebral angiography,</li>
<li>computed tomography (CT)</li>
<li>magnetic resonance imaging (MRI),</li>
<li>Positron emission tomography (PET).</li>
<li>Trans cranial Doppler studies provide information about cerebral blood flow.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Immediate management to relieve increased ICP involves:</li>
<li>decreasing cerebral edema,</li>
<li>lowering the volume of CSF, or</li>
<li>decreasing cerebral blood volume</li>
<li>maintaining cerebral perfusion.</li>
</ul>
<p>These goals are accomplished</p>
<ul>
<li>Administering osmotic diuretics and corticosteroids,</li>
<li>Restricting fluids,</li>
<li>Draining CSF,</li>
<li>Controlling fever,</li>
<li>Maintaining systemic blood pressure and oxygenation,</li>
<li>Reducing cellular metabolic demand</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="monitoring-icp">MONITORING ICP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monitoring-icp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Invasive monitoring of ICP is an important component of management.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The purposes of ICP monitoring are:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To identify increased pressure early in its course (before cerebral damage occurs)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>to quantify the degree of elevation of ICP</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To initiate appropriate treatment,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To provide access to CSF for sampling and drainage,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To evaluate the effectiveness of treatment</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="icp-monitoring-is-done-by">ICP monitoring is done by:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#icp-monitoring-is-done-by" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An intraventricular catheter (ventriculostomy),</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>a subarachnoid bolt,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>an epidural or subdural catheter,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>or a fiberoptic transducer-tipped catheter placed in the subdural space or the ventricle can be used to monitor ICP.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When a ventriculostomy or ventricular catheter monitoring device is used for monitoring ICP, a fine-bore catheter is inserted into a lateral ventricle, usually in the non dominant hemisphere of the brain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The catheter is connected by a fluidfilled system to a transducer, which records the pressure in the form of an electrical impulse.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-process">NURSING PROCESS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Assessment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Initial assessment of the patient with increased ICP includes obtaining a history of events leading to the present illness and other subjective data.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The neurologic examination should be as complete as the patient's condition allows. It includes an evaluation of mental status, LOC, cranial nerve function, cerebellar functioning, reflexes, motor and sensory function.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assess patient level of consciousness using Glasgow coma scale.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Ineffective airway clearance related to diminished protective reflexes (cough, gag)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ineffective breathing patterns related to neurologic dysfunction (brain stem compression, structural displacement)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ineffective cerebral tissue perfusion related to the effects of increased ICP</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Deficient fluid volume related to fluid restriction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Risk for infection related to ICP monitoring</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="potential-complications">POTENTIAL COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#potential-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Brain stem herniation</li>
<li>Diabetes insipidus</li>
<li>SIADH</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="intracranial-surgery">Intracranial Surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intracranial-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>At the end of the lesson the learner should be able to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Define Craniotomy</li>
<li>State indications of craniotomy</li>
<li>State surgical approaches to craniotomy</li>
<li>Explain pre operative and post operative management of a patient undergoing intracranial surgery.</li>
</ol>
<p>A craniotomy involves opening the skull surgically to gain access to intracranial structures.</p>
<ul>
<li>INDICATIONS OF CRANIOTOMY.</li>
<li>to remove a tumor,</li>
<li>relieve elevated ICP,</li>
<li>evacuate a blood clot, and</li>
<li>control hemorrhage.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="approaches-to-craniotomy">APPROACHES TO CRANIOTOMY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#approaches-to-craniotomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>supratentorial approach - above the tentorium into the supratentorial compartment</li>
<li>Infratentorial: below the tentorium.</li>
<li>Transsphenoidal approach; through the mouth and nasal sinuses to gain access to the pituitary gland.</li>
<li>Burr holes: These are circular openings made in the skull by either a hand drill or an automatic craniotome.</li>
</ul>
<p>The tentorium cerebelli or cerebellar tentorium: It is an extension of the duramater that separates the cerebellum from the inferior portion of the occipital lobes.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251228-46e07bc0.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Burr holes are made for exploration or diagnosis.</li>
<li>They may be used to determine the presence of cerebral swelling and injury and the size and position of the ventricles.</li>
</ul>
<p>They are also a means of evacuating an intracranial hematoma or abscess and for making a bone flap in the skull and allowing access to the ventricles for decompression, ventriculography, or shunting procedures.</p>
<p>Other cranial procedures include:</p>
<ul>
<li>craniectomy (excision of a portion of the skull)</li>
<li>cranioplasty (repair of a cranial defect using a plastic or metal plate).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preoperative-management">Preoperative Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preoperative-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Preoperative diagnostic procedures may include CT scanning to demonstrate the lesion and show the degree of surrounding brain edema, MRI provides more resolution, cerebral angiography used to study a tumors blood supply.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anti seizure medication.eg. Phenytoin is prescribed to reduce risk of post operative seizures.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Corticosteroids such as dexamethasone is administered to reduce cerebral edema.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fluids are restricted.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A diuretic agent such as furosemide is given.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Patient is given antibiotics to reduce risk of infection.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preoperative-nursing-management">Preoperative Nursing Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preoperative-nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>This assessment includes evaluating LOC and responsiveness to stimuli and identifying any neurologic deficits, such as paralysis, visual dysfunction, alterations in personality or speech, and bladder and bowel disorders</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assess patient and family understanding of the problem.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Preparation of the patient and family includes providing information about what to expect during and after surgery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The surgical site is shaved immediately before surgery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An indwelling urinary catheter is inserted to drain the bladder during the administration of diuretics and to permit urinary output to be monitored.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A central and arterial line are placed for fluid administration and monitoring of pressures after surgery.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="postoperative-management">Postoperative Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#postoperative-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Postoperatively, an arterial line and a central venous pressure line are in place to monitor and manage blood pressure and central venous pressure.</li>
<li>The patient may be intubated</li>
<li>supplemental oxygen therapy is also given.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="o">O<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#o" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ongoing postoperative management is aimed at:</p>
<ul>
<li>detecting and reducing cerebral edema,</li>
<li>relieving pain</li>
<li>preventing seizures</li>
<li>monitoring ICP.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="reducing-cerebral-edema">REDUCING CEREBRAL EDEMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reducing-cerebral-edema" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Medications to reduce cerebral edema include osmotic diuretics</li>
<li>Dexamethasone may be administered intravenously every 6 hours for 24 to 72 hours which is then changed into oral drugs.</li>
</ul>
<p>RELIEVING PAIN AND PREVENTING SEIZURES</p>
<ul>
<li>Acetaminophen is usually prescribed for fevers</li>
<li>Codeine, given parenterally, is often sufficient to relieve headache. Morphine sulfate may also be used.</li>
<li>Anti seizure medication such as phenytoin is also given.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Monitoring of ICP is done using the Ventricular catheter inserted during surgery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-process">NURSING PROCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessment">Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>After surgery, the frequency of postoperative monitoring is based on the patient's clinical status.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assessing respiratory function is essential.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Arterial blood gas values are assessed frequently.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fluctuations in vital signs are carefully monitored and documented because they indicate increased ICP.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neurologic assessment to include LOC are made to detect increased ICP resulting from cerebral edema or bleeding.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The surgical dressing is inspected for evidence of bleeding and CSF drainage.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The nurse monitors the development of complications; eg. Seizures</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Ineffective cerebral tissue perfusion related to cerebral edema</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Potential for ineffective thermoregulation related to damage to the hypothalamus, dehydration, and infection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Risk for ineffective breathing pattern related to postoperative cerebral edema</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disturbed sensory perception related to periorbital edema, head dressing, endotracheal tube, and effects of ICP.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Body image disturbance related to change in appearance or physical disabilities</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="overview-of-nursing-management-for-the-patient-after-intracranial-surgery">Overview of Nursing Management for the Patient After Intracranial Surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#overview-of-nursing-management-for-the-patient-after-intracranial-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ineffective cerebral tissue perfusion related to cerebral edema</li>
<li>Goal: To maintaining cerebral tissue perfusion.
a. Prevent cerebral edema by assessing patient's level of consciousness; decreased level of consciousness may be the first sign of increased ICP.</li>
</ul>
<p>b. Control postoperative cerebral edema as prescribed.</p>
<p>(1) Administer corticosteroids and osmotic diuretics as prescribed to reduce brain swelling.</p>
<p>(2) Monitor fluid intake; avoid overhydration.</p>
<p>(3) Maintain a normal temperature.</p>
<p>Temperature control may be impaired in certain neurologic states, and fever increases the metabolic demands of the brain.</p>
<ul>
<li>Monitor rectal temperature at specified intervals. Assess temperature of extremities, which may be cold and dry due to impaired heat-losing mechanisms (vasodilation and sweating).</li>
</ul>
<p>Nursing Diagnosis: Risk for ineffective breathing pattern related to postoperative cerebral edema</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>▹</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\triangleright</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4653em;"></span><span class="mord">▹</span></span></span></span></span> Goal: Achievement of adequate respiratory function</p>
<ol>
<li>Establish proper respiratory exchange to eliminate systemic hypercapnia and hypoxia, which increase cerebral edema.</li>
</ol>
<p>a. Unless contraindicated, place the patient in semiprone position to facilitate respiratory gas exchange until consciousness returns.</p>
<p>b. Suction trachea and pharynx cautiously to remove secretions; suctioning can raise ICP.</p>
<p>c. Maintain patient on controlled ventilation if prescribed to maintain normal ventilatory status; monitor arterial blood gas results to determine respiratory status.</p>
<p>d. Elevate the head of the bed 30.5 cm (12 in) after patient is conscious to aid venous drainage of the brain.</p>
<p>e. Administer nothing by mouth until active coughing and swallowing reflexes are demonstrated, to prevent aspiration</p>
<p>Nursing Diagnosis: Disturbed sensory perception (visual/auditory) related to periorbital edema and head dressings</p>
<p>Goal: Compensate for sensory deprivation; prevention of injury</p>
<ol>
<li>Perform supportive measures until the patient can care for self.
a. Change position as indicated; position changes can increase
ICP.
b. Administer prescribed analgesics (codeine) that do not mask the level of responsiveness.</li>
</ol>
<p>Use measures prescribed to relieve signs of periocular edema.</p>
<p>a. Lubricate eyelids and around eyes with petrolatum.</p>
<p>b. Apply light, cold compresses over eyes at specified intervals.</p>
<p>c. Observe for signs of keratitis if cornea has no sensation.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Put extremities through range-of-motion exercises.</li>
</ol>
<p>Evaluate and support patient during episodes of restlessness.</p>
<p>a. Evaluate for airway obstruction, distended bladder, meningeal irritation from bloody CSF.</p>
<p>b. Pad patient’s hands and bed rails to prevent injury.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Reinforce blood-stained dressings with sterile dressing; blood soaked dressings act as a culture medium for bacteria.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Orient patient frequently to time, place, and person</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="potential-complications">POTENTIAL COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#potential-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cerebral edema</li>
<li>Intracranial hemorrhage and hypovolemic shock</li>
<li>Infections</li>
<li>Seizures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-patients-with-cerebrovascular-disorders">Management of Patients With Cerebrovascular Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-patients-with-cerebrovascular-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="specific-objectives">SPECIFIC OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>At the end of the lesson the learner should be able to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Define cerebro vascular disorders</li>
<li>Identify the risk factors for cerebro vascular disorders and related measures for prevention.</li>
<li>Compare the various types of cerebrovascular disorders: their causes, clinical manifestations, and medical management.</li>
<li>Use the nursing process as a framework for care of a patient with cerebrovascular disorder.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="definition">DEFINITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cerebrovascular disorders (CVA) is an umbrella term that refers to any functional abnormality of the central nervous system (CNS) that occurs when the normal blood supply to the brain is disrupted.</li>
<li>These disorders are also referred to as stroke.</li>
</ul>
<p>CVA can be divided into two major categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ischemic stroke; accounts for 85% of all CVA cases. There is vascular occlusion and significant hypo perfusion of the brain tissue.</li>
<li>Hemorrhagic stroke; accounts for 15% of all CVA cases. There is extravasation of blood into the brain tissue or subarachnoid space.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ischemic-stroke">Ischemic Stroke<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ischemic-stroke" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It refers to a sudden loss of function of the brain tissue resulting from disruption of the blood supply to a part of the brain.</li>
<li>This event is usually the result of long-standing cerebrovascular disease.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="aetiology">AETIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The cause of ischemic stroke is mainly formation of a thrombus in the blood vessels occluding the blood flow to the brain.</p>
<p>Based on the cause, ischemic stroke can be subdivided into 5 categories:</p>
<ol>
<li>Large artery thrombotic stroke: They are due to atherosclerotic plaques in the large blood vessels of the brain leading to ischemia and infarction.</li>
</ol>
<p>Small penetrating artery thrombosis; affect one or more vessels and are the most common type of ischemic stroke.
3. Cardiogenic embolic; They are associated with cardiac dysrhythmias, usually atrial fibrillation. Emboli originate from the heart and circulate to the cerebral vasculature, most commonly the left middle cerebral artery, resulting in a stroke.</p>
<p>The last two classifications of ischemic strokes are</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Cryptogenic strokes, which have no known cause, and</li>
<li>other strokes, from causes such as cocaine use, coagulopathies, migraine etc.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In an ischemic brain attack, there is disruption of the cerebral blood flow due to obstruction of a blood vessel.</li>
<li>This disruption in blood flow initiates a complex series of cellular metabolic events referred to as the ischemic cascade.</li>
</ul>
<p>The ischemic cascade begins when cerebral blood flow falls to less than 25 mL/100 g/min. At this point, neurons can no longer maintain aerobic respiration.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The mitochondria must then switch to anaerobic respiration, which generates large amounts of lactic acid, causing a change in the pH level.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This switch to the less efficient anaerobic respiration also renders the neuron incapable of producing sufficient energy needed for cell metabolism and finally the cell ceases to function.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If there is no intervention, the brain cells die leading to brain infarction.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Numbness or weakness of the face, arm, or leg, especially on one side of the body</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Confusion or change in mental status</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Trouble speaking or understanding speech</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Visual disturbances</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Difficulty walking, dizziness, or loss of balance or coordination</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sudden severe headache</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is loss of cognitive, visual, cranial nerves, motor and sensory functioning.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="visual-field-deficits">Visual Field Deficits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#visual-field-deficits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hemianopsia (loss of half of the visual field)</li>
<li>Loss of peripheral vision</li>
<li>Diplopia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="motor-deficits">Motor Deficits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#motor-deficits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Hemiparesis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hemiplegia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ataxia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dysphagia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sensory Deficits</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Paresthesia (occurs on the side opposite the lesion)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Verbal Deficits</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Expressive aphasia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Receptive aphasia</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cognitive-deficits">Cognitive Deficits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cognitive-deficits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Short- and long-term memory loss</li>
<li>Decreased attention span</li>
<li>Impaired ability to concentrate</li>
<li>Poor abstract reasoning</li>
<li>Altered judgment</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Emotional Deficits</li>
<li>Loss of self-control</li>
<li>Emotional lability(sudden changes in mood)</li>
<li>Decreased tolerance to stressful situations</li>
<li>Depression</li>
<li>Withdrawal</li>
<li>Fear, hostility, and anger</li>
<li>Feelings of isolation</li>
</ul>
<p>Assessment and Diagnostic Findings</p>
<ul>
<li>Complete history taking physical and neurologic examination.</li>
<li>Initial assessment focuses on airway patency, respiratory function and cardiovascular Status.</li>
<li>Diagnostic tests such as CT scan to determine if stroke is ischemic or hemorrhagic.</li>
<li>Other tests: EEG, Cerebral angiography and transcranial doppler studies.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors">RISK FACTORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Advanced age, gender, and race are well-known non-modifiable risk factors for stroke.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Modifiable risk factors include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>hypertension,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>cardiovascular disease,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>high cholesterol,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>obesity,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>diabetes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oral contraceptive use (increases risk, especially with coexisting hypertension, smoking, and high estrogen levels)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Smoking</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drug abuse (especially cocaine)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Excessive alcohol consumption</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>MEDICAL MANAGEMENT</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Platelet-inhibiting medications (aspirin, dipyridamole ,clopidogrel and ticlopidine decrease the incidence of cerebral infarction in patients who have experienced CVA from suspected embolic or thrombotic causes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use of Thrombolytic therapy; Recombinant t-PA(tissue plasminogen activator) is a genetically engineered form of t-PA, a thrombolytic substance made naturally by the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It works by binding to fibrin and converting plasminogen to plasmin, which stimulates fibrinolysis of the atherosclerotic lesion.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
<li>
<p>The patient is weighed to determine the dose of t-PA.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The minimum dose is 0.9 mg/kg; the maximum dose is 90 mg.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient is admitted to the intensive care unit, where continuous cardiac monitoring is implemented.</p>
<ul>
<li>
