<li>Other Nursing interventions are done to the patient during and after seizure as discussed above.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="paediatric-conditions-affecting-the-nervous-system">PAEDIATRIC CONDITIONS AFFECTING THE NERVOUS SYSTEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paediatric-conditions-affecting-the-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Objectives</p>
<p>By the end of this section the student will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define and list the common diseases of the nervous system in children.</li>
<li>Identify causes and clinical features of the most common diseases of the nervous system in children.</li>
<li>Describe the nursing care and medical management in relation to the diseases of the nervous system in children.</li>
<li>Identify possible complications that may arise.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hydrocephalus">HYDROCEPHALUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hydrocephalus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is an abnormal condition of fluid around the brain or inside the ventricles.</li>
<li>It is usually a result of an interference with the circulation or absorption of cerebral spinal fluid (CSF).</li>
<li>There are two distinct types of hydrocephalus according to anatomical positions;</li>
<li>communicating and</li>
<li>Non communicating Hydrocephalus.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="communicating-or-extra-ventricular-hydrocephalus">Communicating (or Extra Ventricular) Hydrocephalus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#communicating-or-extra-ventricular-hydrocephalus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In this type of hydrocephalus, the obstruction is outside the ventricular system.</li>
<li>The problem is caused by blockage or occlusion of the sub arachnoid cisterns around the brain stem.</li>
<li>The fluid, which is not being absorbed, compresses the brain and distends the cranial cavity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes">CAUSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Subarachnoid haemorrhage</li>
<li>Bacterial meningitis.</li>
<li>Toxoplasmosis</li>
<li>Diseases of the connective tissues</li>
<li>Sardocoidosis</li>
<li>Head injury</li>
<li>Idiopathic causes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="non-communicating-hydrocephalus">Non Communicating Hydrocephalus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-communicating-hydrocephalus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The obstruction here is within the ventricular systems, leading to interference with the flow of the cerebral spinal fluid to the subarachnoid space</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes">CAUSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Congenital defect developmental, for example, arnod chiari malformation and aqueduct stenosis.</li>
<li>Acquired defects, for example, cerebral abscess, compression of the aqueduct by either aneurysm or haematoma, brain tumour.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessement">ASSESSEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A physical assessment should be undertaken to ascertain the extent and seriousness of the condition, taking into account the infant's age and period of onset.</li>
<li>The head circumference (occipito frontal circumference) should be regularly measured.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Medical treatment with acetazolamide (diamox) is commenced to reduce the production of cerebral spinal fluid in mild cases of hydrocephalus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Repeated lumbar punctures may be performed to maintain normal cerebral spinal fluid pressure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Surgical intervention may also be undertaken, depending on the severity of the condition.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This consists of the removal of obstructions such as tumours, cysts and haemorrhage (haematoma).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A ventriculostomy is done, it involves the destruction of the third and fourth ventricle or the choroid plexus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A radio opaque ventricular catheter is inserted to shunt cerebro spinal fluid (CSF) from the ventricle to another area outside the central nervous system, for example, the abdominal cavity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>These catheters have valves to prevent flow back of blood or any other secretion into the ventricles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Types of valves in use are the Spitz Holter valve system, Hakim shunting system and Heyer Schulte Pudenz catheter.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preoperative-nursing-care">Preoperative Nursing Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preoperative-nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Monitor signs of increased intracranial pressure and report to the surgeon any changes.</li>
<li>Also, continue to frequently measure the head circumference.</li>
<li>Palpate the fontanelles gently for possible separation of sutures and tension.</li>
<li>Vital signs should be taken and recorded (TPR/BP) every one or two hours.</li>
<li>Any deviations should be reported immediately</li>
</ul>
<p>The child's behavioural changes, including persistent cries, should be recorded and reported. Regularly change the child's</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Two hourly position change in bed is done to prevent bed sores.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The neck should be supported when the child is being moved.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The parents are encouraged to participate in their child's care during their hospital stay and in preparation for discharge.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="postoperative-nursing-care">Postoperative Nursing Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#postoperative-nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The preoperative care provided should continue after surgery.</li>
<li>Immediately after surgery, vital signs should be monitored and recorded in one hour intervals, paying particular attention to signs of increasing intracranial pressure.</li>
<li>Other neurological observations, for example, the assessment of the level of consciousness, should also be continued.</li>
</ul>
<p>The dressings on the operation site is checked regularly.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Always ensure that the child lies on the good side to prevent pressure on the shunt valve.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Careful regular feeds should be given.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Parental education is continued from admission until discharge.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Analgesics and antibiotics are also given.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="post-operative-complications">POST OPERATIVE COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-operative-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Meningitis</li>
<li>Vomiting</li>
<li>Infections</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="microcephaly">Microcephaly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#microcephaly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is a relatively uncommon congenital condition where there is a defect in the growth of the brain.</li>
<li>The size of the brain becomes three times smaller than normal.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Foetal radiation</li>
<li>Maternal phenylketonuria, which is an inherited metabolic amino acid phenylalanine because the liver has failed to release an enzyme called phenylalaninase</li>
<li>Congenital infections, for example, syphilis, neonatal herpes, rubella</li>
<li>Intrauterine or neonatal anoxia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The ears are relatively large, the forehead slopes backwards and the head appears smaller.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There is no treatment available for this condition.</li>
<li>Parents are supported and made to understand that.</li>
</ul>
<p>SPINA BIFIDA</p>
<ul>
<li>This is a congenital abnormality, which results from a defect in the formation of the skeletal arch enclosing the spinal cord.</li>
<li>It affects any part of the spinal column and on the skull, but it is more common in the lumbar region.</li>
<li>In spina bifida,the posterior portion of the lamina of one or more vertebrae fails to fuse with or without defective development of the spinal cord, and tends to occur mostly in the lumbar or lumbo sacral region.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>In the milder type (spina bifida oculta), there may be no need for any medical intervention while in the meningocele an meningomyelocele surgical intervention is called for.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pre-and-post-operative-nursing-care">PRE AND POST OPERATIVE NURSING CARE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-and-post-operative-nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The objectives of care should be to prevent infection and injury to the sac, skin damage and urinary tract infection.</li>
<li>These are achieved by performing aseptic technique dressing using warm normal saline until the operation is performed.</li>
<li>The dressing should be changed at least four hourly.</li>
</ul>
<p>The vital signs should be taken and recorded every two hours and any deviation is reported.</p>
<ul>
<li>Continuous assessment of child’s general condition to include musculo skeletal system is done.</li>
</ul>
<p>EPILEPSY</p>
<ul>
<li>Epilepsy can be defined as a neurological condition characterised by recurrent seizures.</li>
<li>A seizure is a sudden attack of altered cerebral function.</li>
<li>An epileptic seizure is the result of altered cerebral function caused by abrupt, abnormal and excessive, uncontrolled repetitive electrical discharges of cerebral neurons.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-three-types-of-epilepsy">The Three Types of Epilepsy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-three-types-of-epilepsy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Petit Mal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Grand Mal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Jacksonian Epilepsy: Characterised by unilateral chronic (sporadic muscular rigidity and relaxation) movements that start in one group of muscles and then systematically spread to adjacent groups of muscles reflecting the match of epileptic activity through the motor cortex.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Investigations, medical and Nursing management is similar to adults.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Common drugs prescribed may be either/or phenobarbitone (luminal) with a dose of 3-6mg/kg body weight or phenytoin sodium (epanutin), with a dose of 10-20mg/kg body weight.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: An epileptic seizure is a medical emergency! Remember the "ABC" rule. Ensure a clear Airway, to enable the patient to Breathe and loosen the clothing to facilitate Circulation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="meningococcal-meningitis">Meningococcal Meningitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meningococcal-meningitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Meningitis means inflammation of the meninges.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The meninges are membranes that cover and protect the brain and spinal cord.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Causative organisms are Neisseria Meningitis (Meningococci).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This micro-organism is intracellular gram negative diplococcus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Meningococcal meningitis is an infectious disease that can be passed from one person to another if meningococci are present in the discharges from the nose and mouth.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Predisposing factors is similar to those in adults</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Usually the onset is acute and sudden</li>
<li>Older children may complain of a headache that becomes severe and spreads down the neck</li>
<li>The patient becomes pyrexial with tachycardia</li>
<li>Rigors are often present</li>
<li>Pain in the back and limbs</li>
</ul>
<p>The patient's neck and possibly the spinal column become stiff/rigid</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Kernig’s sign is positive: patient supine with hip flexed to 90°; pain and inability to fully extend the knee, Kernig’s sign is negative if the patient can fully extend knee</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Due to the fever, convulsions may occur</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The child cries with a high-pitched voice</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anorexia is usually present</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>In very young babies, the anterior fontanelle may bulge outwards instead of positive Kernig's sign</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The child is irritable, drowsy and goes into a comatose state</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Photophobia is usually common and in some cases circulatory collapse with petechial haemorrhage may occur (bleeding spots) on the skin.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cyanosis and vomiting are present.</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-tests">Diagnostic tests<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Begin by taking the patient’s personal history.</li>
<li>A physical examination should follow.</li>
<li>A lumbar puncture is performed to analyse the CSF and may show that polymorph cells are increased.</li>
<li>CSF is turbid in appearance (cloudy), the pressure is raised, glucose level is lower than normal and/or the amount of proteins is raised.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-and-treatment">Nursing Care and Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-and-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The patient is admitted into an isolated cubicle to protect other children</li>
<li>Barrier nursing is instituted for at least the first 48 hours</li>
<li>The room should be quiet and darkened</li>
<li>Shock if present or anticipated, should be effectively managed</li>
<li>Drug therapy should be commenced at once</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-therapy">DRUG THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Crystalline penicillin 300mg (500,000iu)/kg/day, ten times the normal dose given intravenously or intramuscularly three to four hourly until temperature falls, then six hourly for fourteen days.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chloramphenicol (chloromycetin) can also be administered at 100mg/kg/day IM six hourly until a pyrexial and general condition improves usually five to seven days then change to oral syrup for a total of fourteen days.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Phenobarbitone 5mg/kg/day tds is advised for convulsions up to 10mg tds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An ampicillin injection may be given in combination with the chloramphenicol and crystapen.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>END
THANK YOU.</p>
<p>NEUROLOGICAL NURSING</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="module-outcomes">Module Outcomes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-outcomes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Review the anatomy and physiology of the nervous system.</li>
<li>Diagnose, manage and rehabilitate patients with neurological conditions</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="content">Content<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Neurological conditions: Head injury, spinal injury, cerebral vascular accident, epilepsy, meningitis, encephalitis, brain abscess, space occupying lesions, Parkinson's disease, disseminated sclerosis, bell's palsy, myasthenia gravis, Guillen Barre Syndrome.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-and-signs-of-neurologic-disease">SYMPTOMS AND SIGNS OF NEUROLOGIC DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-and-signs-of-neurologic-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Headaches: Headache is an almost universal experience, and one of the most common symptoms in medical practice.</li>
<li>Difficulty walking and falls: Change in gait is a common presenting complaint in neurology.</li>
<li>Dizziness, vertigo, blackouts, collapse and fatigue</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Vertigo - an illusion of movement</li>
<li>Dizziness covers many complaints, from a vague feeling of unsteadiness to severe, acute vertigo</li>
<li>Blackout, like dizziness, is a descriptive term implying either altered consciousness, visual disturbance or falling</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Fatigue is another common symptom of neurological disorders</li>
<li>Spasticity</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cranial-nerves">Cranial nerves<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cranial-nerves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>No</th><th>Name</th><th>Main clinical action</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>I</td><td>Olfactory</td><td>Smell</td></tr><tr><td>II</td><td>Optic</td><td>Vision, fields, afferent light reflex</td></tr><tr><td>III</td><td>Oculomotor</td><td>Eyelid elevation, eye elevation, Adduction, depression in Abduction, efferent (pupil)</td></tr><tr><td>IV</td><td>Trochlear</td><td>Eye in torsion, depression in Adduction</td></tr><tr><td>V</td><td>Trigeminal</td><td>Facial and corneal sensation, muscles of mastication</td></tr><tr><td>VI</td><td>Abducens</td><td>Eye Abduction</td></tr><tr><td>VII</td><td>Facial</td><td>Facial movement, taste fibres</td></tr><tr><td>VIII</td><td>Vestibular</td><td>Balance</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Cochlear</td><td>Hearing</td></tr><tr><td>IX</td><td>Glossopharyngeal</td><td>Sensation - soft palate, taste fibres</td></tr><tr><td>X</td><td>Vagus</td><td>Cough, palatal and vocal cord movements</td></tr><tr><td>XI</td><td>Accessory</td><td>Head turning, shoulder shrugging</td></tr><tr><td>XII</td><td>Hypoglossal</td><td>Tongue movement</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unconsciousness-and-coma">UNCONSCIOUSNESS AND COMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unconsciousness-and-coma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Consciousness means a state of wakefulness with awareness of self and surroundings.</li>
<li>Clouding of consciousness - used more in psychiatry than neurology - means reduced wakefulness and/or self-awareness, sometimes with confusion.</li>
<li>Confusion means altered consciousness - the subject is bewildered and misinterprets his/her surroundings.</li>
<li>Delirium is a state of high arousal (typically delirium tremens). There is confusion and often visual hallucination.</li>
<li>Sleep is normal mental and physical inactivity from which the subject can be roused.</li>
<li>Stupor is an abnormal, sleepy state from which the subject can be aroused by vigorously or repeated stimuli - also used for various psychiatric states, e.g. catatonic and depressive stupor</li>
<li>Coma means unrousable unresponsiveness. The Glasgow Coma Scale for head injury is shown below</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reading-assignment-1">READING ASSIGNMENT 1;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reading-assignment-1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>How to perform neurological examination.</li>
<li>Glasgow coma scale</li>
<li>Neurological investigations</li>
</ol>
<p>NEUROLOGICAL DISORDERS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-head-injury">1. HEAD INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-head-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition: Trauma to the head causing neurological manifestations.</p>
<p>Etiology:</p>
<p>Most common causes include motor vehicle accidents (e.g., collisions between vehicles, pedestrians struck by motor vehicles, bicycle accidents), falls, assaults, sports-related injuries, and penetrating trauma.</p>
<p>The male-to-female ratio for TBI is nearly 2:1, and TBI is much more common in persons younger than 35 years.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-head-injuries">CLASSIFICATION OF HEAD INJURIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-head-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Head injuries can be classified according to. (SAPP)</p>
<ol>
<li>Severity of the injury.</li>
<li>Anatomical classification</li>
<li>Pathological classification-penetrating or blunt injury</li>
<li>Primary and secondary brain injury.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-severity-of-injury">A. SEVERITY OF INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-severity-of-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Severity is assessed by the following methods notably using the Glasgow Coma Scale.</p>
<p>Score below 8 is considered to represent severe head injury</p>
<p>While 8 to 12 is assessed as moderate head injury.</p>
<p>13 to 15 is mild head injury.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-anatomical-classification-injury-can-involve-one-or-more-of-the-following">B. ANATOMICAL CLASSIFICATION; Injury can involve one or more of the following.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-anatomical-classification-injury-can-involve-one-or-more-of-the-following" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>SCALP; This consists of five layers</li>
<li>SKULL INJURIES; Skull fractures are simple or compound.</li>
</ol>
<p>Simple if there is no communication between the fracture and the atmosphere, while the fracture is compound if there is such communication. Skull fractures are classified as follows:</p>
<p>Simple/Closed Fractures (no communication)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>BRAIN INJURY; Injury to the brain is either localised or diffuse and can be either primary or secondary.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="primary-brain-injury">PRIMARY BRAIN INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-brain-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Injury directly due to the insult and occurring at the time of the injury</li>
<li>Brain concussion-temporary physiological disruption of brain function.</li>
<li>Brain contusion-Small petechie and hemorrhages. A contusion is the focal bruising or tearing of cerebral tissue accompanied by parenchymatous hemorrhage and/or local edema.</li>
<li>Brain laceration-obvious deformity</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="localised-injury">Localised injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#localised-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Deformation of the brain at the point of impact. Associated with dural laceration and underlying brain contusion or laceration. Usually there is a localized surrounding oedema around the site of the impact.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diffuse-injury">Diffuse injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diffuse-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This carries a greater risk of damage to the brain and the mechanisms involved in this injury are:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-acceleration-deceleration-injury">a) Acceleration/deceleration injury.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-acceleration-deceleration-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In acceleration injury the head is put into motion from a stand still position, as a result of which the different layers of the brain travels at different velocities with shearing effects and rotation of the brain within the skull.</p>
<p>The shearing stresses between different layers of the brain result in petechial haemorrhages as well as diffuse axonal injury involving the white matter and brain stem.</p>
<p>In deceleration injury the head is brought to a standstill from a moving position as in falls. The same mechanism applies.</p>
<p>The extent of the diffuse injury and the axonal damage determines the outcome.</p>
<p>The more severe the injury is, more brain damage occurs with more axonal injury. This would be associated with higher morbidity and mortality.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-penetrating-injury">b) Penetrating injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-penetrating-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>High velocity or slow velocity injury as a result of penetration with sharp objects.</p>
<p>The base of the skull is thin bone and could easily be penetrated especially in children.</p>
<p>This result in skull base fracture and damage to the brain overlying that area.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="c-compression-injury">c) Compression injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-compression-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The head is compressed between two solid objects as in motor vehicle accidents.</p>
<p>The result is multiple linear fractures particularly in the weak areas of the skull base resulting in multiple cranial nerve injuries.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="secondary-brain-injury">SECONDARY BRAIN INJURY;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-brain-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This results as consequence to the primary brain injury and this includes:</p>
<p>a) INTRACRANIAL HAEMATOMAS. Include epidural haematoma, subdural hematoma, Subarachnoid hemorrhage (The subarachnoid bleeding itself does not usually cause neurologic damage, but hydrocephalus and cerebral); Intraventricular haemorrhage
b) BRAIN OEDEMA
c) INFECTION
d) HYDROCEPHALUS; Hydrocephalus can be caused by blockage of the ventricular system by blood clot in cases of intraventricular haemorrhage
e) CSF LEAK; This is a result of skull fractures crossing the nasal sinuses. In case of ethmoid sinuses - rhinorrhea and fracture internal ear and the middle ear with rupture of tympanic membrane cause otorrhea. Often these leaks are temporary and spontaneous closure within one leak occurs. If it persists then surgical intervention should be considered.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cerebral-ischaemia">Cerebral ischaemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebral-ischaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is common after severe head trauma and is caused by a combination of either hypoxia or impaired cerebral perfusion.</p>
<p>The brain is unable to autoregulate its blood supply with a decrease in blood pressure.</p>
<p>Glutamate excess and free radical accumulation lead to neuronal damage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">DIAGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>History; Detail description of the event leading to injury to the head either from the relatives or from the patient. Aetiology-RTA, Assault, Fall, Missiles, Explosive. Detail of exact mechanism leading to head injury., Site of trauma, any wounds Any history of bleeding, Signs of shock-diziness, confusion, sweating, Any history of loss of consciousness, History of headache, vomiting, Blurring of vision-increased ICP, History of otorrhea or rhinorrhea, Any lateralizing signs-loss of power in the limbs or loss of sensation. History of alcohol or other drug consumption raise the risk of intracranial bleeding and cloud the mental status assessment. The history of previous head injuries-Premorbid illness -DM, HTN, Epilepsy</li>
<li>Physical examination</li>
</ul>
<p>Suspect significant head trauma in any traumatized patient with cranial hematomas or lacerations or with altered sensorium with or without focal neurologic findings.</p>
<p>Obtain complete vital signs</p>
<p>The GCS is the mainstay for rapid neurologic assessment in acute head injury. Both initial and worst GCS post resuscitation scores have correlated significantly with 1-year outcomes following severe head injury</p>
<p>Examine the scalp carefully for evidence of trauma. Inspect the head, and palpate carefully for scalp lacerations, hematomas, ecchymoses, and deformity.</p>
<p>Neurologic Examination</p>
<ul>
<li>INVESTIGATIONS IN HEAD INJURIES; Plain skull x-ray; CT scan,</li>
</ul>
<p>MRI; This examination is useful to show long term effects of head injury. Depending on the availability it also could be used in investigating acute cases.</p>
<p>Beta transferring; This is a test for an enzyme which is only found in CSF. It is the optimum test for CSF leak.</p>
<p>Other Important Baseline Tests; PCV, Urea and electrolytes, Arterial blood gases, Blood alcohol level, Random blood glucose</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>1st is A,B,C,D of resuscitation plus vital signs</li>
</ul>
<p>Airway and cervical spine;</p>
<p>Maintain cervical spine immobilization in all unconscious or symptomatic (neck pain or tenderness) patients.</p>
<p>Inspect mouth remove debris by sweeping through</p>
<p>Chin lift/jaw thrust (tongue is attached to the jaw) and always airway in tongue falling back</p>
<p>Intubations; keep the neck immobilized in neutral position. Intubate all unconscious patients (GCS &lt; 9) to secure airway.</p>
<p>Tracheostomy</p>
<p>Cricothyrotomy</p>
<p>Breathing: Oxygenation and ventilation;</p>
<p>Circulation and arrest of bleeding; Shock" is defined as inadequate organ perfusion and tissue oxygenation. In the trauma patient, it is most often due to haemorrhage and hypovolaemia. The diagnosis of shock is based on clinical findings:</p>
<p>Hypotension, Hypothermia, Tachycardia, Tachypnoea, Cool extremities, Decreased capillary refill, Pallor, Decreased urine production</p>
<ul>
<li>Resuscitation</li>
</ul>
<p>First priority is to stop any obvious bleeding by Sub fascial gauze pack placement and Manual compression on the proximal artery. Carefully applied compressive dressing of the entire injured limb can be done.</p>
<p>Fluids: infuse normal saline initially 2L to run as fast as possible through 2 large bore IV lines</p>
<ul>
<li>Insert urinary catheter and monitor the input and output chart at least 30-50 ml/hour or 0.5/kg/hour of urine flow</li>
<li>Asses by vital signs, pallor, sweating, anxiety, skin warmth, clammy, input and output</li>
<li>Blood transfusion must be considered if the haemoglobin level is less than 7 g/dl and the patient is still bleeding.</li>
<li>Maintain HEAD INJURY OBSERVATION CHART; Monitoring the following in half, hourly or 2 hourly</li>
</ul>
<p>Continuous monitor of level of consciousness; Best eye opening score, Best verbal response score, Best motor response</p>
<p>Vital signs-Pulse, Temperature, BP, Respiratory rate</p>
<p>Pupillary reflexes; Reaction to light, Size of the pupil,</p>
<p>Motor examination of limbs; Spontaneous movement of all the limbs, Paralysis</p>
<p>Monitor danger signs; Severe headache, Vomiting, Convulsions/seizure, Drainage of fluids ear or nose</p>
<ul>
<li>Give analgesia to relieve pain</li>
<li>Administer tetanus toxoid</li>
<li>other general care if patient is unconscious; Bladder care, Bowel care, Physiotherapy chest and limbs, Skin care, Analgesics</li>
<li>Surgical interventions should be carried depending on severity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-head-injury">COMPLICATIONS OF HEAD INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-head-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>CN palsies</li>
<li>Infections</li>
<li>Hydrocephalus</li>
<li>Convulsive disorder/epilepsy</li>
<li>Psychiatric disorders</li>
<li>Cerebrospinal fluid fistulae, either in the form of rhinorrhea or otorrhea</li>
<li>Posttraumatic movement disorders (Tremor, dystonia, parkinsonism)</li>
<li>Post-concussional symptoms e.g. Transient LOC, Bradycardia, Hypertension</li>
<li>Cumulative brain damage ('Punch-drunk syndrome')</li>
<li>Neuroendocrine &amp; metabolic disturbances e.g. Diabetes insipidus.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-spinal-injury">2. SPINAL INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-spinal-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Spinal cord injury (SCI) is an insult to the spinal cord resulting in a change, either temporary or permanent, in its normal motor, sensory, or autonomic function</p>
<p>Spinal injury may involve soft tissues (muscles and ligaments), bones (vertebrae and discs), and neural tissue (spinal cord and nerves). It is important for the primary assessment to establish the presence of an injury and initiate immediate treatment to avoid worsening the primary injury or secondary.</p>
<p>Patients with spinal cord injury usually have permanent and often devastating neurological deficits and disability.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="causes-of-spinal-cord-injuries-include">Causes of spinal cord injuries include<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-spinal-cord-injuries-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Road traffic accidents; Assault; Blunt injury; vascular disorders, tumors, infectious conditions, iatrogenic injuries, developmental disorders.</li>
<li>Penetrating injuries: sharp objects like knives, spears, firearms</li>
<li>Sports injuries; Falling from a height.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bone injury can be stable or unstable and may be associated with neurological manifestations like paraplegia or quadriplegia depending on the level of injury. The injury could be a compression fracture with retropulsion of bone fragments into the spinal cord, causing cord compression or the complete transaction of the cord.</p>
<p>Clinical features</p>
<p>Spinal injury may present as part of the multiply injured patient and caution is needed not to overlook this condition. Neurogenic shock may be present.</p>
<p>History and physical examination: focus on symptoms related to the vertebral column (most commonly pain) and any motor or sensory deficits.</p>
<p>Evaluated for pain, swelling, bruising, or possible mal-alignment</p>
<p>Head that is in an usual position, numbness of or tingling that spreads down an arm, or leg, weakness, difficulty walking, paralysis (loss of movement) of arms or legs, no bladder or bowel control, shock (pale, clammy skin, bluish lips and fingernails, acting dazed or semiconscious, lack of alertness (unconscious), stiff neck, headache or neck pain.</p>
<p>Spinal shock is defined as the complete loss of all neurological function, including reflexes and recal tone, below a specific level that is associated with autonomic dysfunction.</p>
<p>MANAGEMENT;</p>
<p>MANAGEMENT Starts at the site of injury follow:</p>
<p>Principles of management</p>
<ul>
<li>The injury must be recognized.</li>
<li>Take measures to prevent further damage ("secondary" injury) and to detect deteriorating neurologic function so that corrective measures can be taken.</li>
<li>The patient must be maintained in optimal condition to allow the greatest possible nervous system repair and recovery.</li>
<li>Evaluation and rehabilitation of the patient must be actively pursued to maximize the function of surviving but dysfunctional nervous tissue</li>
</ul>
<p>Pre-hospital</p>
<ul>
<li>ABC of resuscitation</li>
<li>Stabilize and immobilize the spine thus cervical column and transport patient on hard board.</li>
<li>Transportation can by ambulances in short distances but if possible air lift is better to avoid movements that would interfere with splinting.</li>
</ul>
<p>Casualty</p>
<ul>
<li>Keep the cervical collar and patient on the backboard</li>
<li>Resuscitation following ABCDE should be done.</li>
</ul>
<p>Airway</p>
<ul>
<li>Clearing of oral secretions and/or debris is essential to maintain airway patency and to prevent aspiration.</li>
<li>Insertion of an oral airway may be all that is required to maintain an airway in some cases. However, intubation may be required in others.</li>
</ul>
<p>Breathing</p>
<ul>
<li>Includes supplementary oxygen for all patients and chest tube thoracostomy for those with pneumothorax and/or hemothorax</li>
</ul>
<p>Circulation</p>
<ul>
<li>Judicious fluid replacement with isotonic crystalloid solution to a maximum of 2 liters is the initial treatment of choice.</li>
<li>Adequate perfusion with the following parameters should be maintained</li>
<li>Systolic blood pressure (BP) should be 90-100 mm Hg. Systolic.</li>
<li>Heart rate should be 60-100 beats per minute in normal sinus rhythm. Hemodynamically significant bradycardia may be treated with atropine.</li>
<li>Urine output should be more than 30 mL/h. Placement of a Foley catheter to monitor urine output is essential</li>
<li>Prevent hypothermia.</li>
</ul>
<p>NB Associated head injury occurs in about 25% of SCI patients. A careful neurologic assessment for associated head injury is compulsory</p>
<p>Inpatient management involves</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Prevention of secondary injury</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oxygen therapy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Splints</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Corticosteroid therapy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Analgesia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bladder care-Condom catheter</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bowel care</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Skin care</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Physiotherapy chest and limbs</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="splints">Splints<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#splints" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Optimal immobilization is obtained by placing the patient supine (face up) on a firm, flat surface (e.g., rigid, long spine board) without a pillow and with lateral motion of the neck restricted by a rigid cervical collar (Philadelphia), lateral neck rolls connected with tape across the forehead, or traction.</p>
<p>Traction is the most effective method.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steroids">Steroids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steroids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>All SCI patients treated within 3 hours of injury with the following steroid protocol: methylprednisolone 30 mg/kg bolus over 15 minutes and an infusion of methyl prednisolone at 5.4 mg/kg/h for 23 hours beginning 45 minutes after the bolus.</li>
<li>Significant improvement in motor function and sensation in patients with complete or incomplete SCIs noted</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="analgesics">Analgesics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#analgesics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Start of opioid analgesia initially then NSAIDS</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bladder-care-condom-catheter">Bladder care: Condom catheter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bladder-care-condom-catheter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Monitor input output of fluids initially. Also if loss of bladder function</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bowel-care">Bowel care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bowel-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Manual evacuation by sweeping through the rectum which cause irritation or the use of enemas (warm soap enema)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ng-tube">NG tube<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ng-tube" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Placement of a nasogastric tube for decompression.</li>
<li>This may also be used for nutritional support.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anti-emetics">Anti emetics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anti-emetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Aspiration pneumonitis is a serious complication in the SCI patient with compromised respiratory function. Antiemetics should be used aggressively</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="skin-care">Skin care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skin-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Prevent pressure sores-Denervated skin is particularly prone to pressure necrosis.</li>
<li>Remove belts and back pocket keys or wallets.</li>
<li>Turn the patient every 1-2 hours.</li>
<li>Pad all extensor surfaces.</li>
<li>Use pneumatic mattresses, continuous motion or ripple mattress.</li>
<li>Good nursing care to prevent wetness-ZNO</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physiotherapy-both-chest-and-limbs">Physiotherapy-both chest and limbs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physiotherapy-both-chest-and-limbs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Prevention of contractures and maintenance of range of motion are important in all patients with spinal cord injury and should begin immediately following the injury.</li>
<li>Chest physiotherapy to prevent pneumostatic pneumonia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">Prognosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Patients with a complete spinal cord injury (SCI) have a less than 5% chance of recovery. If complete paralysis persists at 72 hours after injury, recovery is essentially zero. The prognosis is much better for the incomplete cord syndromes. If some sensory function is preserved, the chance that the patient will eventually be able to walk is greater than 50%</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-spinal-injury">COMPLICATIONS of spinal injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-spinal-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Neurologic deterioration</li>
<li>Pressure sores; - Careful and frequent turning of the patient is required to prevent pressure sores.</li>
<li>Aspiration peumonitis; - Nasogastric decompression of the stomach is mandatory.</li>
<li>Hypothermia; - Prevent hypothermia by using external rewarming techniques and/or warm humidified oxygen</li>
<li>Pulmonary complications in SCI are common. Pulmonary complications of SCI include the following:</li>
<li>Atelectasis secondary to decreased vital capacity and decreased functional residual capacity</li>
<li>Increased work of breathing because of decreased compliance</li>
<li>Decreased coughing, which increases the risk of retained secretions, atelectasis, and pneumonia</li>
<li>Muscle fatigue</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-cerebrovascular-accident">2. CEREBROVASCULAR ACCIDENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-cerebrovascular-accident" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A sudden or gradual interruption of blood supply to a vital centre in the brain is a cerebrovascular accident (CVA), also known as a stroke, brain attack, or central vascular accident.</p>
<p>A CVA can cause complete or partial paralysis or death.</p>
<p>A stroke is focal brain dysfunction due to ischemia. The ischemia may arise from atherosclerotic narrowing of a blood vessel, an embolus, hemorrhage, or other causes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-factors">Risk factors:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypertension, smoking, diabetes mellitus, sickle cell disease, cardiac dysrhythmias, substance abuse, and atherosclerosis. Smoking increases the risk of developing a CVA by two to six times.</li>
<li>The risk also increases for smokers who use birth control pills over an extended period of time. Postmenopausal women are more likely to have CVAs than are younger women.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-cvas">Types of CVAs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-cvas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The two main types of stroke: are ischaemic and haemorrhagic.</p>
<p><strong>NB:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Read and make brief notes on the two types.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms-depend-on-its-cause">Signs and symptoms; depend on its cause;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-depend-on-its-cause" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In some cases of thrombosis and ischemia, the person has had dizzy spells or sudden memory loss for some time before the actual CVA. No pain accompanies these symptoms. So the client ignores them.</li>
<li>A cerebral hemorrhage may give warning. It causes dizziness and ringing in the ears (tinnitus), as well as a violent headache, often with nausea and vomiting.</li>
<li>Embolism usually occurs without warning, although the person has often has a history of cardiovascular disease.</li>
<li>A sudden onset CVA is usually the most severe. This victim loses consciousness; the face becomes red; breathing is noisy and strained. The pulse is slow but full and bounding. Blood pressure is elevated, and the person may be in a deep coma.</li>
<li>Stroke in evolution is a gradual worsening of symptoms of brain ischemia. The coma may deepen progressively until death occurs, or the person may gradually regain consciousness and eventually recover. The longer the time period that the person remains unresponsive, the less likely it is that the person will recover. The first few days after the onset are critical. The responsive person may show sign of memory loss or inconsistency behaviour, he or she may be easily fatigued, lose bowel and bladder control, or have poor balance.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="results-of-cva-some-of-the-major-side-effects-include-the-following">Results of CVA; some of the major side effects include the following;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#results-of-cva-some-of-the-major-side-effects-include-the-following" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hemiplegia: paralysis of one side of the body hemiplegia may affect other functions, such as hearing, general sensation, and circulation: the degree of impairment depends on the part of the brain affected.</li>
<li>Aphasia and dysphasia: Aphasia is a result of damage to the brain's speech centre. Aphasia is a condition in which people are unable to speak. It can be frustrating and frightening because mental functioning usually is unimpaired. Dysphasia is an inability to say what one wishes to say. Many patients regain some power of speech, but others never do. Dysphagia (difficulty swallowing) may also occur.</li>
<li>Brain damage: the extent of brain damage resulting from a CVA determines the client's chances for recovery. If the damage is slight, recovery will be more rapid and complete.</li>
<li>Hemianopsia (hemianopia); hemianopsia is defined as blindness in half of the visual field of one or both eyes.</li>
<li>Pain: usually, after a CVA the client suffers very little pain. Problems such as infection, kidney or bladder calculi (stones) fecal impaction or emotional disturbances may aggravate any existing pain.</li>
<li>Autonomic disturbances; e.g., dilated pupils, high or low blood pressure, or headache. Disturbance this kind may be treated with atropine like drugs.</li>
<li>Personality changes; may be functional or organic. Functional type results from frustration at being unable to speak or walk or form the attitudes of other people. In either case the individual may feel useless or helpless. Organic changes may result from blockage of blood supply to part of the brain. In this instance the person may cry or became easily excited. These conditions cannot be consciously controlled.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical-and-nursing-management">Medical and nursing management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-and-nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>1st is A, B, C, of resuscitation plus vital signs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thrombolytic therapy to resolve the clot (usually heparin, dicumarol or warfarin)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Document every sign of improvement or lack of it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Control blood pressure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Position the unresponsive person on the unaffected side to keep the airway open and prevent aspiration; proper positioning prevents contractures and undue pressure on any part.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid placing the unresponsive person on the back; the tongue may fall back and occlude the airway; secretions may accumulate in the back of the throat.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Provide adequate support for the affected limbs; extremity splints are now widely used. Positioning, support, and splints help prevent contractures.</p>
</li>
<li>
